FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN - WEITERE NACHRICHTEN UND TERMINE:

* GENERAL MOTORS: Die Trennung von Opel kostet den einstigen Mutterkonzern GM einen
Batzen Geld: Der größte US-Autobauer verbuchte in seinem Europageschäft, das an den
französischen PSA-Konzern verkauft wird, im zweiten Quartal einen Verlust von rund 800
Millionen Dollar. Davon entfiel etwa ein Viertel auf das Automobil- und Finanzierungsgeschäft.
Der Rest waren Kosten im Zusammenhang mit der Kündigung von Lieferantenverträgen sowie Verluste
aus dem Verkauf von Leasing- und Finanzierungsverträgen, wie aus der Zwischenbilanz des
Detroiter Konzerns hervorging.

* AUTOKARTELL: EU-Kommissionspräsident Juncker setzt laut "Handelsblatt" das mutmaßliche
Kartell zwischen den großen deutschen Autoherstellern am Mittwoch auf die Tagesordnung der
Kommissionssitzung.

* CITIGROUP setzt sich höhere Ziele. 2020 werde die US-Großbank einen Gewinn von 20
Milliarden Dollar erzielen, stellte Vorstandschef Corbat in Aussicht. Für das laufende Jahr
erwarten Analysten im Schnitt gut 14 Milliarden Dollar. Der Gewinn je Aktie soll um 80 Prozent
steigen - auch dank Aktienrückkäufen.

* McDONALD's hat mit seinen neuen Burgern und Sonderaktionen den Geschmack der Kunden
getroffen. Im zweiten Quartal habe die Schnell-Imbiss-Kette in ihren neueren Restaurants den
höchsten Umsatzzuwachs und die stärkste Kundenfrequenz seit mehr als fünf Jahren erzielt, wie
McDonald's mitteilte. So stiegen die Erlöse konzernweit in den seit mindestens 13 Monaten
geöffneten Restaurants um 6,6 Prozent. Wegen der Übertragung von Geschäften an Franchisepartner
schrumpfte der konsolidierte Umsatz jedoch um 3,4 Prozent auf 6,05 Milliarden Dollar.

* CATERPILLAR: Der weltgrößte Baumaschinenhersteller profitiert von der Erholung der
Rohstoffpreise und einer anziehenden Nachfrage in China. Der Umsatz stieg im abgelaufenen
Quartal binnen Jahresfrist um fast zehn Prozent auf 11,3 Milliarden Dollar, wie der US-Konzern
mitteilte. Der Gewinn kletterte um 46 Prozent auf gut 800 Millionen Euro.

* ELI LILLY: Der US-Pharmakonzern hat dank eines starken Geschäfts mit neuen
Medikamenten seinen Gewinn im zweiten Quartal kräftig gesteigert. Der Nettogewinn erhöhte sich
um mehr als ein Drittel auf 1,01 Milliarden Dollar, wie das Unternehmen mitteilte.

* ZF FRIEDRICHSHAFEN[ZFF.UL] hatte dem "Wall Street Journal" zufolge Interesse an einer
Übernahme von WABCO. Der Autozulieferer habe aber die Gespräche nach einer gründlichen
Buchprüfung (Due dilligence) beendet.

* VERBUND: Österreichs größter Stromkonzern stellt seinen Aktionären trotz eines
Gewinnrückganges im laufenden Jahr eine bis zu einem Drittel höhere Dividende in Aussicht.
Geplant sei eine Ausschüttungsquote zwischen 40 und 45 Prozent bezogen auf das um Einmaleffekte
bereinigte Konzernergebnis, teilte das teilstaatliche Unternehmen mit.

* RBI: Stark schrumpfende Vorsorgen für faule Kredite haben der Raiffeisen Bank
International (RBI) im zweiten Quartal zu einem Gewinnsprung verholfen. Der Konzerngewinn werde
sich im zweiten Quartal auf rund 365 Millionen Euro beinahe verdreifachen, gab das Institut
bekannt.

* Die Chefs führender amerikanischer IT-KONZERNE sollen sich in einem Ausschuss des
Repräsentantenhauses zu den umstrittenen Regeln zur Netzneutralität äußern. Der Vorsitzende des
Ausschusses für Energie und Handel, Walden, setzte die Anhörung für den 7. September an, wie
bekannt wurde.

BLICKPUNKT ZENTRALBANKEN UND KONJUNKTUR:

* GRIECHENLAND gelingt nach drei Jahren die Rückkehr an den Kapitalmarkt. Mit der
Platzierung einer fünfjährigen Staatsanleihe konnte das Land günstiger neue Schulden aufnehmen
als ursprünglich erwartet worden war. Das Wertpapier im Volumen von drei Milliarden Euro wurde
mit einer Rendite von 4,625 Prozent und einem Kupon von 4,375 Prozent bei Investoren
untergebracht.

* USA/RUSSLAND: Die deutsche Wirtschaft fürchtet massive Beeinträchtigungen hiesiger
Unternehmen durch die sich abzeichnenden schärferen US-Sanktionen gegen Russland. Der
Vorsitzende des Ost-Ausschusses der Deutschen Wirtschaft, Büchele, kritisierte, der
Gesetzentwurf des US-Repräsentantenhauses, über den am Dienstag abgestimmt werden soll, drohe
Energiekooperationen mit Russland zu gefährden.

* Der IWF warnt vor einem verfrühten Ausstieg aus der extrem lockeren Geldpolitik in der
Euro-Zone. "Die Rufe aus einigen Ecken nach einem Ausstieg aus der geldpolitischen Stimulierung
sind verfrüht", erklärte der IWF.

* Die Stimmung der US-KONSUMENTEN hat sich im Juli überraschend aufgehellt. Das Barometer
für das Verbrauchervertrauen stieg auf 121,1 Punkte von 117,3 Zählern im Juni, wie das Institut
Conference Board mitteilte.

BREAKINGVIEWS-Despite help from SUVs, GM still isn't there yet - Reuters Breakingviews

{{20170725T161956.368+0000}}BREAKINGVIEWS-Despite help from SUVs, GM still isn't there yet(The author is a Reuters Breakingviews columnist. The opinions expressed are his own.)

By Tom Buerkle

NEW YORK, July 25 (Reuters Breakingviews) - General Motors isn't there yet. The $54 billion U.S. automaker made more money than expected in the second quarter thanks to a shift from cars toward trucks and crossovers. Now, though, it's making too many smaller vehicles. After exiting unprofitable overseas markets, Chief Executive Mary Barra has to slim down at home, too.

Discipline has been Barra's hallmark since becoming the first woman to run a U.S. car company three and a half years ago. An agreement to sell the Opel and Vauxhall business in Europe to France's PSA and a partial exit from the Indian and South African markets have stanched most of GM's international bleeding.

Losses and writedowns on those operations totaled more than $1.4 billion in the quarter, but excising them will boost free cash flow by $1 billion this year to an estimated $7 billion. What's left internationally is in stronger shape. GM made some money in China, where sales rose 1.6 percent, and broke even on an EBIT basis in South America on the back of a nearly 18 percent rise in vehicle sales.

Barra's next challenge is domestic. North American vehicle sales declined 3.4 percent in the second quarter from a year earlier. Bigger products, in particular crossovers, are in high demand, and GM boosted sales of models like the Chevy Equinox by 15 percent. The flipside, though was a 21 percent drop in U.S. passenger-car sales. While much of that reflected a sensible reduction in low-margin sales to rental companies, the company is saddled with far too many cars like the recently revamped compact Cruze and mid-sized Malibu.

Chief Financial Officer Chuck Stevens promised to reduce inventories to a more normal 70-day supply from the current 105 days, but with the overall U.S. market softening that's a moving target. The company said it would slash production by 150,000 vehicles in the second half of the year compared with the first half, a 50 percent larger reduction than Stevens announced just last month.

Washington provided some good news as the Department of Transportation said it may relax fuel-efficiency standards in 2021, a year earlier than planned. That should ease the risk of penalties for an automaker increasingly reliant on gas guzzlers, but it won't shift GM back into growth mode.

On Twitter https://twitter.com/tombuerkle

CONTEXT NEWS

- General Motors on July 25 reported net income attributable to shareholders of $1.7 billion, or $1.09 a share, in the three months ended June, down from $2.9 billion, or $1.81 per share, in the same period a year earlier.

- Excluding losses and writedowns on international operations the company is selling or closing, GM's adjusted earnings for the quarter amounted to $1.89 a share, compared with analysts' consensus expectation of $1.69.

- Revenue was $37 billion in the latest quarter, down 1.1 percent from a year earlier.

- U.S. dealer inventories were up 273,000 from the same period a year earlier, to a 105-day supply. The company said it would reduce inventories to approximately 70 days worth of sales by the end of the year.

- The company reaffirmed guidance for adjusted earnings of $6.00 to $6.50 per share for all of 2017.

- Separately, the U.S. Department of Transportation on July 25 said that it may revise federal fuel efficiency rules beginning in 2021, a year earlier than the Trump administration had previously planned.

FOKUS 1-Opel vor Übernahme durch PSA weiter in den roten Zahlen - Reuters (German)

{{20170725T141839.888+0000}}FOKUS 1-Opel vor Übernahme durch PSA weiter in den roten Zahlen(neu: Angaben zu Opel)

* GM macht in Europa 800 Millionen Dollar Verlust

* Grund sind vor allem Kosten für die Trennung von Opel

* US-Konzern sieht sich trotz Nachfrageflaute in den USA auf Kurs

Detroit/Hamburg, 25. Jul (Reuters) - Die Trennung von Opel kostet den einstigen Mutterkonzern General Motors einen Batzen Geld: Der größte US-Autobauer verbuchte in seinem Europageschäft, das an den französischen PSA-Konzern verkauft wird, im zweiten Quartal einen Verlust von rund 800 Millionen Dollar. Davon entfiel etwa ein Viertel auf das Automobil- und Finanzierungsgeschäft. Der Rest waren Kosten im Zusammenhang mit der Kündigung von Lieferantenverträgen sowie Verluste aus dem Verkauf von Leasing- und Finanzierungsverträgen, wie aus der am Dienstag veröffentlichten Zwischenbilanz des Detroiter Konzerns hervorging. Zu Jahresbeginn war bei den beiden Marken Opel und Vauxhall zusammen ein operativer Verlust von 201 Millionen Dollar angefallen.

In den operativen Zahlen des Konzerns schlägt der Opel-Verlust nicht zu Buche, da GM das Europageschäft als aufgegebenen Bereich führt. Allerdings bekommt der Platzhirsch die Nachfrageflaute in den USA zu spüren. Deshalb kürzt GM die Produktion in Nordamerika in der zweiten Jahreshälfte um 150.000 Fahrzeuge. Der Betriebsgewinn sank im abgelaufenen Quartal auf 2,6 Milliarden Dollar, 400 Millionen weniger als vor Jahresfrist. Grund dafür waren auch Sondereffekte. Der Umsatz gab ebenfalls um 400 Millionen Dollar auf 37 Milliarden Dollar nach. Der Konzern zeigte sich aber zuversichtlich, seine selbstgesteckten Ziele im Gesamtjahr zu erreichen.

Bei Anlegern kam der Ausblick gut an. Die Aktie von GM legte an der New Yorker Börse leicht zu.

Analysten zeigten Verständnis für das Großreinemachen in der Bilanz durch den Opel-Verkauf: "Die wollen die Aufmerksamkeit des Kapitalmarkts natürlich auf die positiven Aspekte lenken", sagte Arndt Ellinghorst vom Investmentberater Evercore ISI. In China laufe es gut, in Lateinamerika habe GM die Gewinnschwelle erreicht, während Konkurrenten dort Geld verlören. Einziger Schwachpunkt ist Europa - und davon trennen sich die Amerikaner gerade.

PEUGEOT SOLL MIT OPEL GLÜCKLICH WERDEN

Der Detroiter Konzern hatte nach immer neuen Verlusten vor einigen Monaten die Reißleine gezogen und will Opel und deren britische Schwester Vauxhall bis Jahresende an Peugeot verkaufen. Die Franzosen wollen damit näher an Europas Branchenführer Volkswagen heranrücken. Peugeot-Chef Carlos Tavares will die Kosten bei Opel senken und den Absatz durch neue, gemeinsam entwickelte Modelle in den nächsten Jahren steigern. So soll Opel spätestens 2020 schwarze Zahlen schreiben.

Der Rückzug aus Europa kommt GM allerdings teuer. Denn nicht nur die Verluste schlagen zu Buche, der US-Konzern muss auch hohe Pensionsverpflichten bei seiner einstigen Tochter schultern, das ist Teil des Deals. Damit machen die Amerikaner mit dem Verkauf unter dem Strich ein Minus.[nL8N1JN4XF]

(Reporter: Nick Carey, Joseph White, bearbeitet von Jan C. Schwartz; redigiert von Kathrin Jones. Bei Rückfragen wenden Sie sich bitte an die Redaktionsleitung unter den Telefonnummern 069-7565 1236 oder 030-2888 5168.) ((jan.schwartz@thomsonreuters.com; +49 40 419 03 4271; Reuters Messaging: jan.schwartz.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net www.twitter.com/REUTERS_DE www.reuters.de))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street en hausse, excepté le Nasdaq, plombé par Alphabet - Reuters (French)

{{20170725T135540.787+0000}}POINT MARCHÉS-Wall Street en hausse, excepté le Nasdaq, plombé par AlphabetPARIS, 25 juillet (Reuters) - Le S&P 500 et le Dow Jones ont ouvert en hausse mardi alors que la saison des résultats s'accélère et que la Réserve fédérale (Fed) entame deux jours de réunion de politique monétaire; les mauvais résultats d'Alphabet font en revanche reculer le Nasdaq.

L'indice Dow Jones <.DJI> gagne 109,66 points, soit 0,51%, à 21.622,83. Le Standard & Poor's 500 <.SPX>, plus large, progresse de 0,31% à 2.477,49, un nouveau record, et le Nasdaq Composite <.IXIC> perd 0,15% à 6.401,31.

Les résultats trimestriels sont surveillés de près par les investisseurs pour savoir si la forte valorisation actuelle du marché est justifiée dans un contexte de faible inflation.

Le S&P 500 se traite à un PER de 18 environ contre une moyenne à long terme de 15.

Les analystes s'attendent à ce que les bénéfices augmentent de 8,8% ce trimestre contre une hausse estimée à 8% au début du mois, d'après le consensus Thomson Reuters I/B/E/S.

Alors que les indices new-yorkais oscillent non loin de leurs plus hauts historiques, l'indice de volatilité VIX <.VIX> perd 1,91% après avoir touché en séance un creux de 25 ans.

La Fed débute ce mardi sa très attendue réunion de politique monétaire bien que beaucoup d'investisseurs estiment que l'institut d'émission ne devrait aborder la question de la réduction de son bilan qu'en septembre et qu'une nouvelle hausse des taux n'apparaît pas vraisemblable avant décembre.

Parmi les statistiques du jour, les prix immobiliers des 20 principales métropoles des Etats-Unis ont augmenté de 5,7% en mai sur un an, soit un rythme moins rapide que prévu, montrent mardi les résultats de l'enquête mensuelle S&P CoreLogic Case-Shiller. [nL8N1JR20S]

Les investisseurs prendront connaissance peu après l'ouverture de l'indice de confiance du consommateur au mois de juillet.

L'indice sectoriel technologique <.SPLRCT> du S&P abandonne 0,46% après les résultats d'Alphabet, de loin la plus mauvaise performance sectorielle de la séance.

La maison-mère de Google cède 3,21% en raison d'une chute de 27,2% de son bénéfice trimestriel imputable à une charge liée à une amende record de 2,4 milliards de dollars imposée par l'Union européenne à sa filiale Google. [nL5N1KF6FN]

Le premier constructeur automobile américain General Motors gagne tout juste 0,42% après avoir publié un bénéfice net trimestriel tiré des opérations poursuivies supérieur au consensus en dépit d'une baisse du chiffre d'affaires et confirmé ses objectifs de 2017. [nL5N1KG47T]

Plus forte progression du Dow Jones, McDonald's gagne 3,77%, l'enseigne de restauration rapide ayant annoncé une hausse plus forte que prévu de ses ventes aux Etats-Unis au deuxième trimestre, grâce à ses promotions sur les boissons et au lancement de nouveaux sandwiches. [nL5N1KG4IX]

Caterpillar gagne 4,01% après avoir enregistré un bénéfice trimestriel et un chiffre d'affaires nettement supérieurs aux attentes et relevé ses objectifs pour la deuxième fois cette année. [nL5N1KG4M8]

Le fabricant de disques durs Seagate chute de 19,18%, plus forte baisse du S&P, après avoir fait état d'un bénéfice trimestriel inférieur aux attentes à 0,38 dollar par action, quand le consensus Thomson Reuters tablait sur 0,98 dollar par action.

Le groupe américain de mode Michael Kors abandonne 3,07% après avoir annoncé un accord pour le rachat du chausseur anglais Jimmy Choo (+16,923% à la Bourse de Londres) pour 896 millions de livres (un milliard d'euros). [nL5N1KG1DZ]

Aux changes, le dollar cède 0,2% face à un panier de devises de référence <.DXY>.

Sur le marché pétrolier, les cours du brut avancent d'environ 1,5% alors que l'Arabie Saoudite s'est engagée à réduire ses exportations.

* Pour les valeurs à suivre, cliquez sur [nL5N1KF6HF]

El beneficio trimestral de General Motors supera las estimaciones - Reuters (Spanish)

{{20170725T135053.041+0000}}El beneficio trimestral de General Motors supera las estimacionesPor Nick Carey y Joseph White

DETROIT, 25 jul (Reuters) - General Motors anunció el martes un beneficio neto trimestral mejor de lo previsto, a pesar de una caída de sus ingresos, y prometió reducir su producción en el segundo semestre para reducir su creciente inventario de vehículos sin vender.

La mayor compañía automovilística de Estados Unidos mantuvo sus previsiones de resultados para 2017, lo que hacía subir más de 1 por ciento sus acciones en las operaciones previas a la apertura de Wall Street.

Los resultados del trimestre excluyen las pérdidas en las operaciones europeas de la automotriz, relacionadas con su marca alemana Opel y con la filial británica Vauxhall, que está siendo vendida al grupo francés PSA .

El anuncio de resultados se produce en un momento en el que a Wall Street le preocupa que la industria automovilística de Estados Unidos esté entrando en una fase de desaceleración tras varios años de sólidas ventas.

Los fabricantes de vehículos han anunciado una caída de la facturación durante cuatro meses consecutivos y los expertos apuntan a los altos inventarios.

La compañía anunció un beneficio neto para el segundo trimestre de 2.400 millones de dólares, o 1,60 dólares por acción, frente a los 2.800 millones de dólares, o 1,74 dólares por papel, registrado en el mismo periodo del año anterior.

Excluyendo extraordinarios, la compañía ganó 1,89 dólares por acción. Analistas esperaban en promedio que los beneficios trimestrales de GM llegaran a 1,69 dólares por acción.

Los ingresos trimestrales de GM fueron de 37.000 millones de dólares, un descenso respecto a los 37.400 millones de dólares registrados en el mismo periodo del año anterior y por debajo de la facturación de 40.100 millones de dólares prevista por analistas.

(Reporte de Nick Carey. Editado en español por Marion Giraldo) ((Mesa de edición en español +562 24374447. Twitter: @ReutersLatam))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

ACTUALIZA 1-Utilidad de General Motors supera estimaciones, promete reducir inventarios  - Reuters (Spanish)

{{20170725T132413.716+0000}}ACTUALIZA 1-Utilidad de General Motors supera estimaciones, promete reducir inventarios (Amplía información, añade firmas de autores)

Por Nick Carey y Joseph White

DETROIT, 25 jul (Reuters) - General Motors reportó el martes unas ganancias netas a partir de operaciones continuas mejores de lo previsto, a pesar de una caída de sus ingresos, y prometió reducir la producción de autos en el segundo semestre a fin de disminuir los crecientes inventarios de vehículos en las concesionarias.

La mayor automotriz de Estados Unidos mantuvo sus previsiones de utilidades para el 2017, en una noticia que hacía subir en más de 1 por ciento sus acciones en las operaciones previas a la apertura de Wall Street.

Los resultados del trimestre excluyen las pérdidas en las operaciones europeas de la automotriz, relacionadas a su marca alemana Opel y a la unidad británica Vauxhall, que está siendo vendida al grupo francés PSA .

La divulgación de resultados se produce en momentos en que Wall Street se muestra temeroso de que la industria automotriz de Estados Unidos esté ingresando a una fase de desaceleración luego de varios años de robustas ventas.

Los fabricantes de vehículos han reportado una baja de la facturación por cuatro meses consecutivos y expertos apuntan a los altos inventarios.

Hasta fines de junio, GM Co tenía 150 días de suministros de autos para vender, por encima de la provisión de 90 días con la que contaba en abril. La compañía dijo el martes que los inventarios en concesionarias en el segundo trimestre aumentaron en 273.000 unidades frente al mismo periodo de 2016.

GM planea recortar su producción en Norteamérica en 150.000 vehículos en el segundo semestre del 2017, en relación al primer semestre, dijo el martes el presidente financiero de la compañía, Chuck Stevens.

Además, GM aún tiene previsto reportar una ganancia de entre 6 y 6,50 dólares por acción en el 2017.

La automotriz reportó una ganancia neta para el segundo trimestre de 2.400 millones de dólares, o 1,60 dólares por acción, que se compara con la utilidad de 2.800 millones de dólares, o 1,74 dólares por papel, registrada en el mismo periodo del año anterior.

Excluyendo ítems extraordinarios, la compañía ganó 1,89 dólares por acción. Analistas esperaban en promedio que los beneficios trimestrales de GM llegaran a 1,69 dólares por acción.

Los ingresos trimestrales de GM se ubicaron en 37.000 millones de dólares, un descenso respecto a los 37.400 millones de dólares registrados en el mismo periodo del año anterior y por debajo de la facturación de 40.100 millones de dólares prevista por analistas.

(Reporte de Nick Carey. Editado en español por Marion Giraldo) ((Mesa de edición en español +562 24374447. Twitter: @ReutersLatam)) ((REUTERS MG JL GB/))Copyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

U.S. may revise 2021 fuel efficiency standards - Reuters News

{{20170725T130904.240+0000}}U.S. may revise 2021 fuel efficiency standardsJuly 25 (Reuters) - The U.S. Transportation Department said on Tuesday it may revise the 2021 model year fuel efficiency requirements as it reviews the Obama administration vehicle emissions rules a year earlier than previously disclosed.

In March, President Donald Trump ordered a review of U.S. vehicle fuel-efficiency standards from model year 2022 through 2025. U.S. regulators said in a notice published Tuesday they are preparing a new environmental impact statement and could adopt lower standards through 2025.

USA-Les valeurs à suivre à Wall Street (actualisé) - Reuters (French)

{{20170725T130510.870+0000}}USA-Les valeurs à suivre à Wall Street (actualisé)(Actualisé avec McDonald's, Caterpillar, General Motors, Seagate, United Technologies et cours avant-Bourse)

NEW YORK, 25 juillet (Reuters) - Principales valeurs à suivre mardi à Wall Street où les contrats à terme sur les indices de référence signalent une ouverture en hausse, à l'exception du Nasdaq en recul :

* GENERAL MOTORS a publié mardi un bénéfice net trimestriel tiré des opérations poursuivies supérieur au consensus en dépit d'une baisse du chiffre d'affaires et le premier constructeur automobile américain a confirmé ses objectifs de 2017. L'action prend 2,6% à 36,75 dollars en avant-Bourse. [nL5N1KG47T]

* CATERPILLAR prend 4,5% en avant-Bourse après avoir publié mardi un bénéfice trimestriel et un chiffre d'affaires nettement supérieurs aux attentes, soutenus par le dynamisme de ses activités dans la construction en Chine, et a relevé ses objectifs pour la deuxième fois de l'année.[nL5N1KG4M8]

* ALPHABET a annoncé lundi soir une chute de 27,7% de son bénéfice trimestriel, en raison d'une charge liée à une amende record de 2,4 milliards de dollars (2,1 milliards d'euros) imposée par l'Union européenne à sa filiale Google, mais son chiffre d'affaires a augmenté de 21% [nL5N1KF6FN]. Le titre cède 3% dans les échanges d'avant-Bourse.

* MCDONALD'S gagne 3,1% en avant-Bourse, l'enseigne de restauration rapide a annoncé mardi une hausse plus forte que prévu de ses ventes aux Etats-Unis au deuxième trimestre, grâce à ses promotions sur les boissons et au lancement de nouveaux sandwiches. [nL5N1KG4IX]

* DUPONT - Le groupe chimique américain a publié mardi un bénéfice trimestriel en baisse mais meilleur que prévu, grâce aux bonnes performances de ses activités pour l'agriculture, avant sa fusion avec DOW CHEMICAL qu'il pense finaliser le mois prochain. [nL5N1KG39V]

Le titre prend 1,2% en avant-Bourse.

* UNITED TECHNOLOGIES a annoncé un chiffre d'affaires en hausse de 2,7% au deuxième trimestre grâce à une hausse des ventes de trois de ses quatre divisions. L'action gagne 1% en avant-Bourse. [nL5N1KG4VJ]

* BIOGEN a fait état mardi d'un chiffre d'affaires trimestriel en hausse de 6,4%, grâce notamment à une forte demande pour son nouveau traitement de l'amyotrophie spinale, Spinraza. L'action prend 4,5% en avant-Bourse.

* ELI LILLY cède 1,5% en avant-Bourse malgré la publication d'un bénéfice trimestriel supérieur aux attentes pour le groupe pharmaceutique.

* ANADARKO PETROLEUM , première compagnie pétrolière à publier ses résultats trimestriels, a annoncé lundi soir une perte plus lourde qu'attendu et prévenu qu'elle réduirait son budget d'investissement de 300 millions de dollars (257 millions d'euros) cette année en raison de la déprime des cours du brut. L'action cède 2,7% en avant-Bourse.

* MICHAEL KORS - Le groupe américain de mode gagne 2,8% après avoir annoncé un accord pour le rachat du chausseur anglais Jimmy Choo pour 896 millions de livres (un milliard d'euros). [nL5N1KG1DZ]

* SEAGATE TECHNOLOGY - Le fabricant de disques durs chute de 16,7% en avant-Bourse après avoir fait état d'un bénéfice trimestriel inférieur aux attentes à 0,38 dollar par action, quand le consensus Thomson Reuters tablait sur 0,98 dollar par action.

* TECHNIPFMC a annoncé lundi une révision de ses comptes du premier trimestre en raison "d'erreurs importantes". L'action cotée à Paris du groupe de services pétroliers perd plus de 8%, la plus forte baisse du CAC 40 <.FCHI> et du Stoxx 600 <.STOXX>. Celle cotée à Wall Street recule de 8% en avant-Bourse. [nL5N1KG1EX]

* BARNES & NOBLE . Le fonds activiste Sandell Asset Management a fait pression mardi sur la chaîne américaine de librairies pour qu'elle se mette en vente. Le titre grimpe de 17,6% dans les échanges d'avant-Bourse à Wall Street. [nL5N1KG3S7]

* CITIGROUP , recapitalisée à trois reprises durant la crise financière de 2007-2009, organise mardi une journée investisseurs pour la première fois depuis mai 2008, quatre semaines après le feu vert de la Fed lui permettant de mieux rémunérer ses actionnaires.

* AT&T et FACEBOOK publient leurs résultats après la clôture.

Lucro da GM supera estimativas de Wall St e empresa promete reduzir estoques  - Reuters (Portuguese, Brazil)

{{20170725T125127.207+0000}}Lucro da GM supera estimativas de Wall St e empresa promete reduzir estoques DETROIT, 25 Jul (Reuters) - A General Motors divulgou nesta terça-feira lucro líquido trimestral melhor que o esperado nas operações continuadas, apesar de queda na receita, e prometeu reduzir a produção no segundo trimestre para diminuir o crescente estoque de veículos que não vendidos.

A maior montadora dos Estados Unidos manteve sua previsão de lucro para 2017. As notícias elevaram as ações da GM em mais de 1 por cento antes da abertura dos mercados.

A divulgação de resultados acontece em um momento em que Wall Street está preocupada com a possibilidade da indústria automotiva norte-americana estar entrando em uma recessão. As montadoras têm divulgado queda nas vendas pelos últimos quatro meses consecutivos.

Os analistas estão preocupados com estoque de veículos não vendidos da GM, refletindo decisões para armazenar pickups e veículos utilitários esportivos antes dos planejado fechamentos de fábricas para equipá-las para produção de novos modelos.

A GM planeja cortar a produção norte-americana em 150 mil veículos no segundo semestre de 2017 em comparação com o primeiro semestre, disse o diretor financeiro Chuck Stevens a repórteres na terça-feira.

A GM divulgou lucro líquido de 2,4 bilhões de dólares ou 1,60 dólar por ação no segundo semestre, uma queda ante os 2,8 bilhões, ou 1,74 dólar por ação, um ano antes. Excluindo itens únicos, a empresa divulgou lucro por ação de 1,89 dólar.

Nesta mesma base, analistas em média esperavam lucro por ação de 1,69 dólar no trimestre.

A empresa divulgou receita de 37 bilhões de dólares no trimestre, ante 37,4 bilhões de dólares um ano antes e abaixo dos 40,1 bilhões de dólares esperados por analistas.

A GM disse que ainda espera lucrar entre 6 dólares e 6,50 dólares por ação em 2017.

(Por Nick Carey)

((Tradução Redação São Paulo 56447764))

General Motors spürt Nachfrageflaute - Gewinn sinkt - Reuters (German)

{{20170725T121707.258+0000}}General Motors spürt Nachfrageflaute - Gewinn sinktDetroit, 25. Jul (Reuters) - Der führende US-Autohersteller General Motors bekommt eine niedrigere Nachfrage nach seinen Fahrzeugen zu spüren. Im abgelaufenen Quartal sank der Nettogewinn auf 2,4 Milliarden Dollar, 400 Millionen Dollar weniger als vor Jahresfrist. Der Umsatz gab ebenfalls um 400 Millionen Dollar auf 37 Milliarden Dollar nach, wie GM am Dienstag mitteilte. Zugleich zeigte sich der Konzern aber zuversichtlich, seine selbstgesteckten Ziele im Gesamtjahr zu erreichen.

An der Börse kam das gut an: Die Aktien legten im vorbörslichen Handel mehr als zwei Prozent zu.

In den USA mehren sich die Anzeichen für einen Abschwung in der Autobranche. Die großen Hersteller verzeichnen seit vier Monaten einen Absatzrückgang. Die Lager sind voll, die GM-Händler hatten nach GM-Angaben 273.000 Fahrzeuge mehr in ihren Hallen stehen als vor Jahresfrist.

Die Zahlen zum Europa-Geschäft sind nach dem Verkauf von Opel nicht mehr in den Quartalsergebnissen enthalten. GM hatte im Frühjahr bekanntgegeben, die schwächelnde deutsch-britische Tochter an den Peugeot-Hersteller PSA abzugeben.

General Motors quarterly profit falls - Reuters News

{{20170725T113417.121+0000}}General Motors quarterly profit fallsDETROIT, July 25 (Reuters) - General Motors Co on Tuesday reported a lower quarterly net profit from continuing operations due to lower vehicle sales and restructuring charges, but results beat Wall Street expectations.

Daimler directors to meet over alleged German auto cartel - sources - Reuters News

{{20170725T091714.748+0000}}Daimler directors to meet over alleged German auto cartel - sourcesFRANKFURT/HAMBURG, July 25 (Reuters) - Daimler's supervisory board will meet on Wednesday and seek answers about whether German carmakers were part of a club that was allegedly involved in anti-competitive behaviour, sources familiar with the matter said on Tuesday.

European Union and German antitrust regulators are investigating whether BMW , VW , Porsche, Audi and Mercedes-Benz owner Daimler held meetings to discuss suppliers, prices and standards to the disadvantage of foreign carmakers. [nL5N1KD0AW]

While carmaker associations commonly discuss how to implement new emissions standards and technologies, the question being probed by regulators is whether talks among the German manufacturers constituted anti-competitive behaviour.

German magazine Der Spiegel reported on Friday that German carmakers colluded to fix the prices of diesel emissions treatment systems using industry committees. Companies found guilty of breaching EU cartel rules face fines of as much as 10 percent of their global revenue.

These auto industry committees operated outside of the official industry association VDA, which counts foreign suppliers and foreign-owned carmakers like Opel among its members.

In a statement, VDA said compliance policies for members preclude anti-competitive behaviour, adding the issues being probed by regulators "relate to a format which was not part of the VDA and its work."

"A couple of months ago manufacturers approached VDA, to integrate further development, standard setting and norm setting activities into VDA," the association said, adding existing members were being consulted about how to deal with the matter.

(Reporting by Ilona Wissenbach and Jan Schwartz; Writing by Edward Taylor; Editing by Mark Potter) ((Edward.Taylor@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1187;))

Guten Morgen von Reuters am Dienstag, den 25. Juli - Reuters (German)

{{20170725T045114.915+0000}}Guten Morgen von Reuters am Dienstag, den 25. JuliTOP NEWS:

* VOLKSWAGEN: Die Besitzer von VW-, Audi-, Skoda- und Seat-Fahrzeugen mit
manipulierten VW-Dieselmotoren müssen sich einem Medienbericht zufolge auf den Verlust ihrer
Zulassung einstellen, wenn sie das Software-Update ablehnen. Dies gehe aus einem Schreiben des
Kraftfahrt-Bundesamtes hervor, wie "Focus Online" berichtete. In einigen Fällen könnte dies
bereits ab August sein.

* DAIMLER ist einem Medienbericht zufolge mit seiner Selbstanzeige bei den
Wettbewerbsbehörden wegen des mutmaßlichen Kartells in der Autoindustrie VW zuvorgekommen. Der
Daimler-Konzern habe sich deutlich früher als Volkswagen an die Behörden gewandt, berichteten
"SZ", NDR und WDR. Damit könne der Stuttgarter Autohersteller darauf hoffen, ohne Strafe
davonzukommen, sollte die EU-Kommission Geldbußen wegen verbotener Absprachen verhängen.

* ALPHABET: Eine milliardenschwere Rekordstrafe der EU-Kommission hat dem
Google-Mutterkonzern einen Gewinneinbruch eingebrockt. Im abgelaufenen Quartal brach der
Überschuss verglichen mit dem Vorjahr um 28 Prozent auf 3,5 Milliarden Dollar ein. Der Umsatz
stieg jedoch unter anderem dank eines boomenden Werbegeschäfts auf Smartphones und Tablets um 21
Prozent auf 26 Milliarden Dollar. Zudem zahlte sich auch der Fokus auf die Video-Tochter YouTube
aus.

=========================================

FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN:

DAX:

* VOLKSWAGEN: "Wir werden in Zukunft Elektroautos mit Reichweiten von bis zu 600 Kilometern
anbieten können - zum Preis eines vergleichbaren Dieselfahrzeugs", sagte Konzernchef Müller der
"Heilbronner Stimme". Beim Dieselskandal sieht der Manager Fortschritte. "Wir sind schon sehr
weit gekommen, allein in Europa sind mehr als drei Viertel der Fahrzeuge nachgerüstet."

* DAIMLER: Mercedes-Benz kehrt zum Ende der Saison 2018 der Rennserie DTM den
Rücken. Stattdessen wolle man in der Elektroserie Formel E an den Start gehen, teilte das
Unternehmen mit.

* DEUTSCHE BANK: Der Chef des chinesischen Mischkonzerns und
Deutsche-Bank-Großaktionärs HNA, Tan, hat Berichte über wachsenden Druck von Banken und
Regulierungsbehörden auf sein Unternehmen zurückgewiesen. HNA unterhalte nach wie vor enge
Arbeitsbeziehungen zu seinen wichtigsten Wall-Street-Banken wie JPMorgan, UBS und Morgan
Stanley, sagte Tan. Spekulationen, dass einige Banken ihre Kredite an die Gruppe zurückfahren
würden, seien nicht wahr.

* BAYER: Die Online-Aktivistengruppe Avaaz hat die EU-Wettbewerbsbehörde
aufgerufen, die Übernahme von MONSANTO durch BAYER zu untersagen. Eine entsprechende
Petition habe mehr als eine Million Unterzeichner, so die Gruppe in einem Brief an
EU-Wettbewerbskommissarin Vestager.

MDAX:

* COVESTRO<1COV.DE>: Q2

* HOCHTIEF: Q2

TECDAX:

* DRILLISCH: Aktionäre stimmen auf einer a.o. HV über die Übernahme durch UNITED
INTERNET ab

* AIXTRON: Q2

SDAX:

* TELE COLUMBUS bekommt einen neuen Vorstandsvorsitzenden. CEO Verhelst scheide
nach knapp sieben Jahre zum 1. Februar 2018 aus persönlichen Gründen aus dem Unternehmen aus.
Seine Nachfolge als CEO übernimme Timm Degenhardt.

FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN - WEITERE NACHRICHTEN UND TERMINE:

* FACEBOOK/GOOGLE/TWITTER: Die Europäische Union hat den Druck auf
Facebook, Google und Twitter erhöht, damit diese die Nutzungsbedingungen ihrer sozialen
Netzwerke an EU-Recht anpassen. Die drei Unternehmen wurden im Juni von der Kommission
schriftlich aufgefordert, bis zum 20. Juli verbesserte Vorschläge zu unterbreiten, wie aus den
Schreiben hervorgeht, die Reuters einsehen konnte.

BLICKPUNKT ZENTRALBANKEN UND KONJUNKTUR:

* EZB: Die Erholung im Euro-Raum greift nach Einschätzung von EZB-Direktor Mersch immer mehr
um sich. Der aktuelle Schwung erhöhe die Chancen, dass der Aufschwung stärker ausfalle als
erwartet, sagte er auf einer Veranstaltung in Singapur laut Redetext.

* EZB: Nach Einschätzung eines hochrangigen EZB-Experten wandern inzwischen womöglich wieder
mehr Investorengelder zurück in riskantere Anleihen der südlichen Euro-Länder. "Vielleicht ist
eine Sache, die wir jetzt sehen, dass dies zu passieren beginnt," sagte der Leiter der
volkswirtschaftlichen Abteilung der Europäischen Zentralbank (EZB), Frank Smets. Es sei etwas
überraschend, dass sich nach den jüngsten Kursausschlägen am Anleihenmarkt die
Renditeunterschiede eingeengt hätten

=========================================

BLICKPUNKT POLITIK:

* NAHOST/JERUSALEM: Im Streit um die Zugangskontrollen zum Tempelberg in Jerusalem lenkt die
israelische Regierung offenbar ein. Das Kabinett beschloss am Dienstag nach mehrstündiger
Beratung den Abbau der von den Palästinensern heftig kritisierten Metalldetektoren. Stattdessen
sollten andere Sicherheitsvorkehrungen installiert werden, die als weniger störend empfunden
würden, erklärte die Regierung. Die Entscheidung markiert eine Kehrtwende des
Ministerpräsidenten Benjamin Netanjahu.

* DEUTSCHLAND/WAHLUMFRAGE: Zwei Monate vor der Bundestagswahl kann die Union den Abstand auf
die SPD in der Sonntagsfrage weiter vergrößern. In einer Umfrage des Meinungsforschungsinstituts
INSA für die "Bild"-Zeitung kommen CDU und CSU auf 37,5 Prozent (+1,5), während die SPD bei 25
Prozent verharrt. Die Linke steigert sich um einen Prozentpunkt auf 10,5 Prozent, Grüne (6,5
Prozent) und FDP (8,5 Prozent) bleiben unverändert. Die AfD verliert einen Prozentpunkt und ist
mit neun Prozent der Wählerstimmen nicht mehr drittstärkste Kraft.

* POLEN: Der polnische Präsident Duda hat sein Veto gegen Teile der umstrittenen
Justizreform verteidigt. An zwei von drei der vorgeschlagenen Gesetze seien Änderungen
erforderlich, um deren Verfassungsmäßigkeit sicherzustellen, sagte Duda in einer
Fernsehansprache. Er werde in Kürze seine eigenen Vorschläge präsentieren.

What to Watch in the Day Ahead - Tuesday, July 25 - 路透新闻

{{20170724T184009.000+0000}}What to Watch in the Day Ahead - Tuesday, July 25(The Day Ahead is an email and PDF publication that includes the day's major stories and events, analyses and other features. To receive The Day Ahead, Eikon users can register at [DAY/US]. Thomson One users can register at RT/DAY/US. All times in ET/GMT)

The U.S. Federal Open Market Committee begins its two-day meeting on interest rate policy. Many analysts and investors expect the Federal Reserve to announce that it will begin reducing its bond portfolio at its September meeting, but will await firmer indications on the timing of this effort at this week's meeting.

DuPont is expected to report a rise in second-quarter profit due to higher demand for seeds. As Dow and DuPont are nearing the completion of their deal, investors will keep an eye out for leadership of the combined company. Any news on divestiture for regulatory approval would also be looked upon.

General Motors releases second-quarter results amid investor concern about declining demand in the United States. The company has already flagged higher-than-projected costs related to the sale of Opel to PSA.

3M Co, which makes Scotch tape and Post-it notes, is expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second quarter, led by higher sales in its industrials unit, which makes tapes and adhesives for the automotive, aerospace, electronics and packaging industries.

The S&P CoreLogic Case-Shiller composite index of 20 metropolitan areas which measures U.S. single-family home prices, is expected to have increased 5.8 percent in May. (0900/1300) The U.S. Conference Board is expected to show that its consumer confidence index slipped to a reading of 116.5 in July, from 118.9 in June. (1000/1400) The Federal Reserve Bank of Richmond issues manufacturing and services indices for July. (1000/1400)

Caterpillar Inc, the heavy machinery manufacturer, is expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second quarter, helped by improving demand in the construction and energy industries. Investors will look for an update on full-year financial forecast, which the company raised in April.

Investors will focus on any developments in the protracted permit talks with Indonesia's government when Freeport-McMoRan reports second-quarter results. Freeport, the world's biggest publicly traded copper miner, is in a costly dispute over future rights at its Grasberg mine. Some analysts expect ongoing problems at Grasberg, the world's second biggest copper mine, could hit profits.

Amgen reports second-quarter results with hopes for a rebound in sales of its big-selling rheumatoid arthritis drug, Enbrel, after a disappointing first quarter. Investors will also be looking for more information on a regulatory setback for Amgen's experimental osteoporosis drug, romosozummab, and for a potential update to its full-year forecasts.Eli Lilly & Co is likely to report higher second-quarter earnings, according to Thomson Reuters data, helped by strong sales of its diabetes treatments. Investors will look for comments on the changing landscape of the healthcare industry from Lilly, which won a years-long patent dispute over its top-selling cancer drug, Alimta, earlier this month.

Biogen Inc is also expected to report its second-quarter results before the bell. Investors will focus on the performance of Biogen's pricey new spinal muscular atrophy drug, Spinraza, amid slowing sales of its best-selling multiple sclerosis treatment, Tecfidera. Separately, HCA Healthcare Inc reports second-quarter results. The company's quarterly earnings are likely to be higher due to an increase in patient volume and cost control. Investors will look for comments from the largest U.S. for-profit hospital operator about the Senate Republican's failed move to repeal Obamacare. Investors will also focus on the company's future M&A plans.

Mid-cap health insurer Centene Corp, which primarily focuses on government-sponsored plans, is set to report higher second-quarter earnings due to acquisitions and increased membership. Investors will focus on how the health insurer keeps its medicaid business profitable amid changing dynamics of the health insurance industry under President Donald Trump's administration.

AT&T Inc is expected to post a fall in second-quarter revenue as the largest U.S. TV provider looks to close its $85.4 billion acquisition of Time Warner. According to sources, AT&T will run its wireless and DirecTV satellite television businesses separately from Time Warner's media assets. Analysts will be looking out for any commentary regarding this.

Interpublic Group Of Companies Inc is expected to report a rise in second-quarter revenue due to an improvement in business in its biggest market, the United States.

McDonald's Corp is expected to report its second-quarter results. The company is seeking to reverse years of traffic declines at its U.S. restaurants with the introduction of cooked-to-order Quarter Pounders made from fresh beef, higher-end signature crafted sandwiches and mobile and kiosk ordering, while also testing home delivery. Chipotle Mexican Grill Inc also reports second-quarter results. Chipotle's fragile recovery from a string of food safety lapses in 2015 likely will overshadow its quarterly financial report, which lands just days after the chain briefly closed a Virginia restaurant due to norovirus and a video of mice in a Dallas restaurant went viral.

Domino's Pizza Inc is expected to report a second-quarter profit above analysts' average estimate as higher demand boosts same-store sales. The company, which has posted double-digit sales growth over the past four quarters, has managed to stay ahead of U.S. rivals such as Yum Brands' Pizza Hut and McDonald's by introducing options such as mobile ordering and voice ordering.

PulteGroup Inc, the third biggest U.S. homebuilder, is expected to post increases in second-quarter profit and revenue as strong housing demand drives higher home sales. Investors will look for details on the company's financial forecast.

Jet engine and elevator maker United Technologies Corp posts second-quarter results. Investors will be looking for updates on solving problems with its Pratt & Whitney engines, which have delayed delivery of some Airbus planes.

Akamai Technologies Inc reports second-quarter results. The online content distributor is expected to report a rise in second-quarter revenue, driven by strong demand for its security services. However, Akamai has been experiencing a slowdown in its media delivery business after some of its large customers shifted to their own delivery networks, raising concerns about the company's revenue.

Texas Instruments Inc reports second-quarter results. The chipmaker is expected to post a rise in quarterly revenue, helped by demand for analog and embedded chip products from the automotive and industrial markets.

Newmont Mining Corp announces second-quarter results. Investors will watch to see if Newmont, the world's second-largest gold producer, announces financial results that deliver on its forecasts, but no big surprises are expected in the report.

Canadian National Railway Co will report second-quarter results, as investors look for guidance on volumes and operating efficiency as fuel prices grow.

Citigroup holds its first day-long conference for investors since 2008. Nearly a decade after Citigroup suspended "Investor Day" conferences during the financial crisis, bank executives say they are ready to again meet in an auditorium with big investors and securities analysts to talk about their strategy to boost shareholder returns. The conference comes after Chief Executive Mike Corbat failed to meet performance targets that he set in 2013 shortly after directors fired the previous CEO and put Corbat in charge.

Brazil's FGV is expected to release its consumer confidence index for July. Consumer confidence in Brazil has risen in recent months as a surprise inflation drop allowed the central bank to cut interest rates more aggressively, easing the burden on debt-laden families. (0700/1100) Mexico's national statistics agency is expected to say that annual retail sales increased 2.9 percent in May. (0900/1300) Argentina's economic activity is likely to expand 3.1 percent in May, compared with a 0.6 percent increase in April. (1500/1900)

LIVECHAT- FED WATCH Reuters reporters and editors tracking the Federal Reserve take questions on the economics, politics, trade matters and rates policies facing America's central bank and others whose decisions drive markets day in and day out. (0930/1330) To join the Global Markets Forum, click here http://bit.ly/1kTxdKD

(Compiled By Shradha Singh in Bengaluru; Editing by Maju Samuel) ((Shradha.Singh@thomsonreuters.com))

Guten Abend von Reuters am Montag, den 24. Juli - Reuters (German)

{{20170724T155535.074+0000}}Guten Abend von Reuters am Montag, den 24. JuliTOP NEWS:

* VOLKSWAGEN ruft unter dem Druck der Kartellvorwürfe als erster betroffener
Hersteller seinen Aufsichtsrat zusammen. Aufsichtsratschef Pötsch habe das 20-köpfige Gremium
für Mittwoch zu einer außerordentlichen Sitzung einberufen, sagte ein Sprecher. Dabei werde es
um die am Wochenende bekanntgewordenen Vorwürfe illegaler Absprachen von VW, AUDI, PORSCHE,
DAIMLER und BMW in der Fahrzeugentwicklung gehen, sagte ein Insider. Die
EU-Kommission hatte einen Bericht des "Spiegel" bestätigt, wonach sie dem Verdacht solcher
Absprachen nachgeht. An der Börse gingen Autoaktien zu Wochenbeginn auf breiter Front auf
Talfahrt.

* Die TÜRKEI macht im Streit mit Deutschland über Demokratie, Wahlkampf-Veranstaltungen und
Besuchsrechte einen Rückzieher: Vier Tage nach dem von Bundesaußenminister Gabriel angekündigten
Kurswechsel in der Türkeipolitik teilte die Regierung in Ankara am Montag mit, Ermittlungen
gegen rund 700 deutsche Firmen wegen angeblichen Terrorverdachts fallenzulassen. Keine Bewegung
zeichnete sich allerdings in den Auseinandersetzungen über inhaftierte Deutsche ab, die in der
Türkei ebenfalls unter Terrorverdacht einsitzen.

* POLENS Präsident Duda hat nach wochenlangen Protesten und einer Konfrontation mit der
Europäischen Union hat die umstrittene Justizreform gestoppt. Duda kündigte am Montag sein Veto
gegen zwei der drei Gesetze an, mit der die regierende nationalkonservative Partei Recht und
Gerechtigkeit (PiS) das Justizwesen grundlegend umbauen will. Er verwies das Gesetzespaket zur
Überarbeitung zurück an das Parlament. Der stellvertretende Regierungschef Morawiecki zeigte
sich von der Entscheidung "enttäuscht und überrascht". Die Opposition sprach dagegen von einem
Sieg des Volkes über den Versuch, die Gewaltenteilung abzuschaffen.

* MÄRKTE: Die Kartellvorwürfe gegen deutsche Autokonzerne haben dem Aktienmarkt zu schaffen
gemacht. Der Dax<.GDAXI> rutschte unter Führung der Autowerte um 0,3 Prozent auf 12.208 Punkte
ab. Der EuroStoxx50<.STOXX50E> schloss kaum verändert. Zum Handelsschluss in Europa tendierten
die großen US-Indizes uneinheitlich: Während der Dow-Jones<.DJI>-Index 0,3 Prozent im Minus lag,
waren der S&P500<.SPX>-Index und der Nasdaq-Composite<.IXIC> minimal im Minus. Mit 1,1684 Dollar
notierte der Euro zeitweise so hoch wie zuletzt im August 2015.

FIRMEN UND BRANCHEN:

DAX:

* SIEMENS: Russland zeigt sich im Streit über Turbinen des deutschen Hersteller
auf der annektierten Halbinsel Krim gelassen. Für russische Unternehmen bestehe kein Risiko,
sagte Energieminister Nowak. Die Produkte, die SIEMENS geliefert habe, könnten auch von anderen
Unternehmen erworben werden. Die Turbinen waren für ein Projekt auf der südrussischen Halbinsel
Taman bestimmt, sind nun aber auf die von Russland annektierte ukrainische Krim gelangten.
SIEMENS sieht sich als Opfer seines russischen Kunden.

* Mit der Warnung vor einer Rückkehr der FLÜCHTLINGSKRISE nach Deutschland stößt
SPD-Kanzlerkandidat Schulz auf Zustimmung der AfD. Schulz habe "ausnahmsweise mal recht", sagte
AfD-Spitzenkandidat Gauland am Montag. Es handele sich aber um "unglaubwürdige
Lippenbekenntnisse". Schulz hatte gewarnt, die EU müsse Italien dringend Flüchtlinge abnehmen.

W. aus Sachsen ermittelt nun die Generalbundesanwaltschaft. Ein Sprecher der Behörde sagte am
Montag in Karlsruhe, das Verfahren sei von der Dresdner Staatsanwaltschaft übernommen worden.

Menschen getötet worden, darunter viele Polizisten. 52 weitere Menschen seien verletzt worden.
Zu der Tat bekannten sich die pakistanischen Taliban.

Vertretern im Wahlkampf verteidigt. "Ich hatte keine rechtswidrigen Kontakte", schrieb er in
einer Erklärung vor seiner Aussage vor Kongress-Ausschüssen.

Opel defends inclusion of employee leases in sales data - Reuters News

{{20170722T150744.334+0000}}Opel defends inclusion of employee leases in sales dataFRANKFURT, July 22 (Reuters) - German carmaker Opel, which is being bought by French rival PSA Group from General Motors , said on Saturday that its sales figures included cars pre-registered by Opel and leased by company workers and pensioners and their families.

Car trade publication Automobilwoche, in an article due to appear in its July 24 edition, said the company only reached a market share of 7.1 percent in a first-half 2017 survey compiled by Automobilwoche because it included pre-registrations and heavy discounts.

The trade weekly said if these so-called push-channels were not included, Opel would only have a market share of 4.5 percent and would be overtaken by Skoda, Volkswagen's Czech unit .

An Opel spokesman said there was nothing wrong with the count and because Opel was a German company, the number of such sales was necessarily higher than for importers of foreign cars.

"In pre-registrations, Opel includes cars that employees and former employees (a total of 60,000 entitled people) may lease for themselves or their family members," he said.

"We are glad that our staff stand behind Opel and that the number of our cars used privately by employees and their families is constantly on the increase," he added.

Automobilwoche said that the market shares of other companies such as BMW , Mercedes and VW reflected push-channels to a far lesser extent.

(Reporting by Vera Eckert, Editing by Mark Trevelyan) ((vera.eckert@thomsonreuters.com; +49 69 7565 1228; Reuters Messaging: vera.eckert.thomsonreuters.com@reuters.net))

Keywords: OPEL SALES/COUNTCopyright (c) 2017 Thomson Reuters

What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, July 24 - 路透新闻

{{20170721T200342.534+0000}}What to Watch in the Week Ahead and on Monday, July 24(The Day Ahead is an email and PDF publication that includes the day's major stories and events, analyses and other features. To receive The Day Ahead, Eikon users can register at [DAY/US]. Thomson One users can register at RT/DAY/US. All times in ET/GMT.)

WEEKAHEAD

Investors, next week, will focus on the Federal Reserve's two-day policy meeting that will begin on Tuesday. Expectations that the U.S. central bank will leave key overnight borrowing costs unchanged partly fed the decline in short-term interest rate volatility. Markets will work through another spate of economic figures that include gross domestic product, data on labor costs, durable goods figures, consumer confidence index, single-family home prices and data on mortgage applications. On Friday, the gross domestic product for the second quarter is expected to have increased at a 2.6 percent annual rate. On the same day, the Employment Cost Index is likely to have gained 0.6 percent in the second quarter. On Tuesday, the S&P CoreLogic Case-Shiller composite index of 20 metropolitan areas, which measures U.S. single-family home prices, is expected to have increased 5.8 percent in May. In a separate report on the same day, the U.S. Conference Board is expected to show a drop in its consumer confidence index. The index is expected to have slipped to a reading of 116.5 in July, from 118.9 in June. The Mortgage Bankers Association's weekly index for mortgage applications is on the tap for Wednesday. On Thursday, overall orders for durable goods, items ranging from toasters to aircraft that are meant to last three years or more, are expected to have increased 2.6 percent in June.

A slew of Dow 30 companies, including chemicals conglomerate DuPont, industrial conglomerate United Technologies Corp, Scotch tape and Post-it notes maker 3M Co, Exxon Mobil Corp, Chevron and the heavy machinery manufacturer Caterpillar Inc are scheduled to report results next week. Exxon Mobil is expected to post profit in the second quarter on Friday. Chevron also reports its second-quarter results on the same day. DuPont is expected to report a rise in second-quarter profit on Tuesday, due to higher demand for seeds. As Dow and DuPont are nearing the completion of their deal, investors will keep an eye out for leadership of the combined company. 3M Co is also expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second-quarter on the same day, led by higher sales in its industrials unit, which makes industrial tapes and adhesives, and caters to automotive, aerospace, electronics and packaging industries. Meanwhile, Caterpillar is expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second quarter on Tuesday, helped by improving demand in the construction and energy industries. Separately, when United Technologies will post its second-quarter results on Tuesday, investors will be looking for updates on solving problems with its Pratt & Whitney engines, which have delayed delivery of some Airbus planes.

Amazon.com Inc is expected to report a rise in quarterly revenue on Thursday, helped by growth in its retail and cloud computing businesses. Investors will look for more details on Amazon's surprise $13.7 billion deal to buy upscale grocer Whole Foods Market, which could upend the already struggling U.S. retail industry. Investors will also focus on Amazon's current-quarter forecast, which will include sales from its annual Prime day shopping event that expanded to China, India and Mexico this year.

Facebook Inc reports second-quarter results on Wednesday. The social media giant is expected to post a rise in profit and revenue driven by its fast-growing mobile ad business. Facebook is searching for new types of advertising features to supplement its main revenue streams that it expects to cool off this year. Any update on its plans to beef up its features would be interesting.

On Tuesday, General Motors releases its second-quarter results, amid investor concern about declining demand in the United States. The company has already flagged higher-than-projected costs related to the sale of Opel to PSA. Ford Motor Co reports second-quarter results on Wednesday, the first since new CEO Jim Hackett took charge. He could elaborate on his plans to reevaluate Ford operations and speed decisions.

MasterCard Inc, the world's second-biggest payments processor is expected to report a rise in second-quarter profit on Thursday, with higher cross-border volumes growth. However, costs are expected to rise due to the two acquisitions it made in Q1, VocaLink and NuData Security. Investors will also look for any update on the card company's progress to start operations in China.

Eli Lilly & Co is likely to report higher second-quarter earnings on Tuesday, according to Thomson Reuters data, helped by strong sales of its diabetes treatments. Biogen Inc is also expected to report its second-quarter results before the bell on the same day. Investors will focus on the performance of Biogen's pricey new spinal muscular atrophy drug, Spinraza, amid slowing sales of its best-selling multiple sclerosis (MS) treatment Tecfidera. Meanwhile, Merck & Co. Inc will report its second-quarter results on Friday. Investor focus will be on the performance of the company's high-profile cancer drug Keytruda as the drugmaker reports second-quarter results amid rising competition in the lung cancer market. AbbVie Inc will also report second-quarter results on the same day, that is likely to be helped by increased sales of its flagship drug, Humira. Investors will also look for comment on its cancer drug Imbruvica, which analysts expect to become an important revenue driver for the drugmaker. Celgene Corp's second-quarter results scheduled for release on Thursday, are likely to be helped by sales of its blockbuster cancer drug, Revlimid, whose sales have slowed in the past few quarters.

Health insurer Anthem Inc reports second-quarter results before the bell on Wednesday in the wake of the failed Republican effort to overhaul or repeal Obamacare. Investors will look for comments from Anthem, which sells Blue Cross Blue Shield plans in 14 states, about the state of the health insurance industry. Mid-cap health insurer Centene Corp, which primarily focuses on government-sponsored plans, is set to report higher second-quarter earnings on Tuesday, due to acquisitions and increased membership. Investors will focus on how the health insurer keeps its medicaid business profitable amid changing dynamics of the health insurance industry under President Donald Trump's administration.

Boston Scientific Corp reports second-quarter results on Thursday. Investors will likely focus on Boston Scientific's heart device, Lotus valve system's performance in comparison to Medtronic Plc's CoreValve TAVI system. Analysts expect the company to outperform its large-cap med device peers as the company's robust pipeline products will contribute meaningfully to revenue.

AT&T is expected to post a fall in second-quarter revenue on Tuesday, as the largest U.S. TV provider looks to close its $85.4 billion acquisition of Time Warner. According to sources, AT&T will run its wireless and DirecTV satellite television businesses separately from Time Warner's media assets, analysts will be looking out for any commentary regarding this. On the wireless front, AT&T is likely to struggle to keep its subscribers amid stiff competition. Meanwhile, Verizon Communications Inc reports second-quarter results on Thursday. The No. 1 U.S. wireless carrier is expected to report its fifth straight quarter of revenue declines. The company, which has been facing stiff competition from smaller rivals such as T-Mobile and Sprint, are likely to lose customers to other players in the market.

Texas Instruments Inc reports second-quarter results on Tuesday. The chipmaker is expected to post a rise in quarterly revenue, helped by demand for analog and embedded chip products from the automotive and industrial markets.

Twitter Inc reports second-quarter results on Thursday. The microblogging service is expected to report its second fall in revenue in its latest quarter since its debut. Chief Executive Jack Dorsey, whose leadership has been questioned amidst stagnating user growth, is looking to shake things up for the company to cope with stiff competition from Facebook and Snapchat. However, Twitter reported better-than-expected growth in its monthly active users last quarter and any sign of that momentum continuing will be closely monitored as the company looks to woo users with a revamped interface and wider offerings.

Coca-Cola Co is expected to report second-quarter results on Wednesday. Coca-Cola is looking to cut costs, mainly by reducing 1,200 jobs, and invest in growing its non-carbonated beverage business amid falling demand for fizzy drinks globally. The company in April forecast a smaller decline in 2017 adjusted profit than it had previously expected.

McDonald's Corp is expected to report its second-quarter results on Tuesday. The company is seeking to reverse years of traffic declines at its U.S. restaurants with the introduction of cooked-to-order Quarter Pounders made from fresh beef, higher-end signature crafted sandwiches and mobile and kiosk ordering, while also testing home delivery. Chipotle Mexican Grill Inc also reports second-quarter results on the same day. Chipotle's fragile recovery from a string of food safety lapses in 2015 likely will overshadow Tuesday's quarterly financial report, which lands just days after the chain briefly closed a Virginia restaurant due to norovirus and a video of mice in a Dallas restaurant went viral.

Hershey Co reports second-quarter results on Wednesday. The Hershey Kisses and Cadbury chocolates maker's second-quarter sales is expected to grow as the company has been launching a flurry of new products to keep up with demand from snack-loving consumers in the United States, its home turf. The company has also been keeping a tight lid on costs to help mitigate loss from its China business.

General Dynamics Corp, the maker of Gulfstream jets, is expected to report higher revenue for the second quarter on Wednesday, helped by stable demand for its business jets in North America. Investors will look for an update on full-year financial forecast. U.S. weapons maker Northrop Grumman Corp is also expected to report higher profit and revenue for the second quarter on Wednesday, helped by higher sales in its aerospace unit, which makes parts for F-35 fighter jets, drones and spacecraft. Investors will look for an update on full-year financial forecast. Raytheon Co, the maker of Tomahawk missiles, is expected to report higher revenue in the second quarter on Thursday, as it sees increased demand for its products fueled by a pro-defense Trump administration and U.S. allies. Investors will look for an update on 2017 financial forecast. D.R. Horton Inc, the No.1 U.S. homebuilder is expected to report a rise in fourth-quarter revenue and profit on Wednesday, helped by higher home sales. An improving job market has supported U.S. housing demand but homebuilders continue to face land and labor shortages. Investors will look for the company's financial forecast and details on its pending deal with real estate developer Forestar Group Inc. On Tuesday, PulteGroup Inc, the third biggest U.S. homebuilder is expected to post increases in second-quarter profit and revenue as strong housing demand drives higher home sales. Investors will look for the details on the company's financial forecast.

Nasdaq, the transatlantic exchange operator, will report its second-quarter earnings on Wednesday. Net income is expected to rise, helped by higher trading revenue. Expenses are expected to fall. Nasdaq also bought Canadian stock trading venue CXC and news distribution company Marketwired last year and will continue to benefit from the acquisition. The exchange industry is in the midst of a wave of consolidation as companies seek to move more trading onto fewer technology platforms to boost profit margins.

The New York Times Co reports second-quarter results on Thursday. The newspaper publisher is expected to swing to a quarterly profit from a year-earlier loss, as it benefits from higher digital subscriptions. The Times has been investing in marketing to sign up more digital subscribers even as it cuts costs through restructuring that job cuts. It offered buyouts to some of its newsroom employees in May in an effort to streamline editing and production systems.

Citigroup holds its first day-long conference for investors since 2008 on Tuesday. Nearly a decade after Citigroup suspended "Investor Day" conferences during the financial crisis, bank executives say they are ready to again meet in an auditorium with big investors and securities analysts to talk about their strategy to boost shareholder returns. The conference comes after Chief Executive Mike Corbat failed to meet performance targets that he set in 2013 shortly after directors fired the previous CEO and put Corbat in charge.

Canada's second-largest oil and gas producer, Suncor Energy Inc, reports second-quarter earnings on Wednesday. Suncor has endured lower-than-expected oil prices and problems at the Syncrude oil sands plant, in which it is the majority owner. Investors will look for updates to Suncor's strategy and progress reports on Syncrude and the company's new Fort Hills and Hebron projects.

Alaska Air Group reports second-quarter results on Wednesday. Analysts expect Alaska Air's results to improve from the preceding quarter's steep earnings drop. The West Coast airline in December bought rival Virgin America in a $2.6 billion deal to become the fifth-largest U.S. carrier.

The main economic event in Canada next week will be monthly gross domestic product for May, released on Friday. The report will likely support analysts' expectations that the economy maintained its momentum in the second quarter after a strong start to the year. Stronger-than-expected growth could also underscore expectations that the Bank of Canada will hike interest rates again in the coming months.

ON MONDAY

Google's parent company, Alphabet Inc, is expected to report increases in second-quarter profit and revenue, helped by strong advertising sales on mobile devices and for video content. The company's cloud computing business has long trailed those of Amazon.com Inc and Microsoft Corp, although it has managed to win some major deals. Investors will look for updates on Google's plan to beef up its cloud business, as its dependence on search has been a worry.

Six ministers from OPEC and non-OPEC nations Kuwait, Venezuela, Algeria, Saudi Arabia, Russia and Oman as well as OPEC's secretary general will meet in St Petersburg, Russia to discuss the current situation in the oil market. Traders predicted prices would hold near current levels ahead of Monday's meeting between key OPEC and non-OPEC producers in St. Petersburg. The market has been watching reports that Saudi Arabia, the world's largest crude producer, is considering an additional supply cut to bring markets into balance.

The Markit U.S Manufacturing Purchasing Managers' Index (PMI) for July is expected to come in at 52.1 compared with 52.0 in the previous month. Markit services PMI for July is expected at 54.3. (0945/1345) The National Association of Realtors is likely to say that existing home sales dropped to 5.57 million units in June. U.S. home resales unexpectedly rose in May to 5.62 million units. (1000/1400)

Hasbro Inc, the No.2 U.S. toymaker, is expected to post second-quarter revenue above analysts' estimates, helped by higher shipments of toys based on the "Transformers: The Last Knight" and "Spider-Man: Homecoming" movies.

Halliburton Co is expected to report a profit in the second quarter, compared to a year-ago loss, helped by increased demand for its pressure pumping and well-construction services. U.S. shale producers have been putting more rigs to work, buoyed by oil prices that are hovering close to $50. Investors will see whether Halliburton can keep up the optimistic tone set by market leader Schlumberger.

A newly established U.S.-UK trade and investment working group will hold its first meeting in Washington to scope out plans for a potential free trade agreement between the two countries after Brexit. The meeting will take place in Washington at the U.S. Trade Representative's office and will include Liam Fox, the UK secretary for international trade, and Donald Trump's trade czar Robert Lighthizer.

Statistics Canada is expected to show a slower rise in Canadian wholesale trade for May. Canadian wholesale trade is expected to rise 0.5 percent in May after a 1.0 percent gain in April. (0830/1230)

CORRECTED-UPDATE 1-UAW talking to GM about impact of car sales slump on U.S. jobs - Reuters News

{{20170721T153813.512+0000}}CORRECTED-UPDATE 1-UAW talking to GM about impact of car sales slump on U.S. jobs(In paragraph 11, corrects to "Bank of America Merrill Lynch auto analyst John Murphy" instead of "Morgan Stanley auto analyst")

By Paul Lienert and Nick Carey

July 20 (Reuters) - The president of the United Auto Workers union said on Thursday the union is talking with General Motors Co about the potential threat to plants and jobs from slumping U.S. car sales.

"We are talking to (GM) right now about the products that they currently have" at underused car plants such as Hamtramck in Michigan and Lordstown in Ohio, and whether they might be replaced with newer, more popular vehicles such as crossovers, Dennis Williams told reporters.

"We are tracking it (and) we are addressing it," Williams added.

GM has cut shifts at several U.S. plants this year as inventories of unsold cars have ballooned. Industry analysts said more jobs could be at risk as the automaker wrestles with permanently shrinking production of small and midsized sedans.

GM is reviewing whether to cancel at least six passenger cars in the U.S. market after 2020, including the Chevrolet Volt hybrid, which could be replaced in 2022 with a new gasoline-electric crossover model, Reuters has learned from people familiar with the plans [nL1N1K81FQ].

Other GM cars at risk include the Buick LaCrosse, Cadillac CT6, Cadillac XTS, Chevrolet Impala and Chevrolet Sonic, sources said.

Some analysts have singled out GM's Hamtramck plant in Detroit as one of the most vulnerable because of plummeting car sales.

The plant, which opened in 1985, builds four slow-selling models: Buick LaCrosse, Chevrolet Impala, Cadillac CT6 and Chevrolet Volt.

In the first half, it built fewer than 35,000 cars, down 32 percent from the same period in 2016, according to suppliers familiar with GM's U.S. production schedule. The typical GM assembly plant builds 200,000-300,000 vehicles a year.

GM must "create some innovative new products" to replace slow-selling sedans "or start closing plants," said Sam Fiorani, vice president of AutoForecast Solutions.

The auto maker already has begun to shift future production plans from cars to trucks, according to Bank of America Merrill Lynch auto analyst John Murphy. He estimates that fewer than 10 percent of the new vehicle models that GM will introduce over the next four years will be passenger cars, with the rest divided among trucks, SUVs and crossovers.

GM plans to add production of the new Cadillac XT4 crossover next year to its Malibu sedan plant in Fairfax, Kansas.

The company is cutting production in the short term rather than dumping cars into rental car fleets at little or no profit, company executives have said.

However, the long-term shift in demand toward SUVs calls into question the future of factories GM currently has dedicated to building sedans, analysts said.

GM said it does not comment on future products.

Alan Batey, president of GM's North American operations, told Reuters in an interview: "I don't think we have too many" sedans."

GM SAYS 'IN A GOOD PLACE'

Batey said GM intends to reduce overall inventories to around 75 days by year-end from 105 currently. "We're in a good place to have a good 2017," he said.

The shift toward SUVs, fueled by cheap gasoline, is putting pressure on nearly all major automakers in the United States to simultaneously shift short-term production plans and rework long-term product programs that drive capital spending over several years.

Sales of GM passenger cars plunged 17 percent in the first half and 36 percent in June, exceeding the industry-wide declines of 12 percent in the first half and 14 percent in June, according to Automotive News.

GM dealers ended June with as much as six months supply of certain models. Two months is considered normal.

"There could be some consolidation" of passenger car production in fewer U.S. plants, said Jeff Schuster, senior vice president of LMC Automotive. "GM doesn't need all the sedans it has today."

Lyft accelerates efforts to develop self-driving cars - Reuters News

{{20170721T150001.424+0000}}Lyft accelerates efforts to develop self-driving carsBy Heather Somerville

SAN FRANCISCO, July 21 (Reuters) - Lyft Inc has formed a self-driving car division, company executives said, a bold investment for the second-largest U.S. ride-services firm as it jockeys for position in the highly competitive autonomous vehicle race.

The executives said on Thursday the company would soon open a facility in Palo Alto, California, that would eventually be staffed by "several hundred" engineers. Lyft engineers will collaborate there with autonomous vehicle experts from other companies to build self-driving systems.

"We are putting down the accelerator significantly on investment on this," Raj Kapoor, chief strategy officer for Lyft, told reporters at its San Francisco headquarters.

The move marks a striking strategy change for Lyft, which said previously it would leave the building of self-driving systems to others while allowing partners to test their autonomous cars in Lyft's ride-hailing network.

Lyft previously announced partnerships with Alphabet's self-driving division, Waymo, technology company Nutonomy, and automakers General Motors Co and Jaguar Land Rover . Lyft's new effort could put it in direct competition with some of those partners.

The company, which will not be manufacturing the actual cars, offered no time line for its self-driving ambitions. Executives said Lyft would share data from its self-driving efforts with other companies joining the collaboration.

Lyft does not have a permit to test autonomous cars in California, according to the state Department of Motor Vehicles. The company plans to launch a pilot with Nutonomy in Boston by year-end.

Building autonomous driving systems is a complicated and expensive endeavor, and brings a new layer of complexity to Lyft. Unlike its far larger rival, Uber Technologies Inc , which has tackled everything from food delivery to flying cars, and expanded overseas, Lyft has operated strictly as a ride service for people in the United States.

Lyft's 700,000 drivers complete more than 200 million rides and 1.2 billion miles (1.9 billion km) a year in the 350 cities where it operates, which executives said gave the company detailed knowledge of traffic patterns, bridges, construction and other roadway data critical for building autonomous systems.

"The one thing that is very, very key is the scale that we have," said Luc Vincent, vice president of engineering.

None of those miles have been driven with autonomous technology, experts point out, meaning Lyft will be starting from scratch in a business where Waymo, Tesla and Uber have been operating for years.

"It does still take a lot to do this, even if there is lots off-the-shelf technology, to engineer them together and create systems and put them in a vehicle," said Jeremy Carlson, an automotive analyst at IHS Markit.

Lyft's new push comes as Uber is facing a lawsuit from Waymo over alleged theft of trade secrets relating to self-driving technology designs.

Lyft in April raised $600 million in new funding [nL1N1HJ1J3]. The company has begun preparations for an initial public offering, sources close to the company told Reuters.

(Reporting by Heather Somerville; Editing by Peter Cooney) ((Heather.Somerville@thomsonreuters.com;)(415)(321-2320; Reuters Messaging: Follow me on Twitter @heathersomervil))
